id=\"section_550.38\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/192648499/\">(38)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">The fees chargeable on bail-bonds given in pursuance of an order made by a Court or Magistrate under any section of the Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898 (V of 1898).</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-subsection\" id=\"section_550.39\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/84530165/\">(39)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">The fees chargeable under Article (6) of Schedule II of the Court fees Act, 1870 (VII of 1870), on supratnamas in criminal proceedings.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-subsection\" id=\"section_550.40\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/150227026/\">(40)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">The fees chargeable under (b) of Article I to Schedule II of the Court-fees Act, 1870 (VII of 1870), on all applications or petitions to Criminal Courts on behalf of the state.</span></span></section></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_551\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/149342595/\">551.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-intro\"><span class=\"akn-p\">The attention of the Courts is invited to the provisions of sub-sections (1) and (2) of Section 371 of the Code of Criminal Procedure. The words \"free of cost,\" in that section grant an exemption only from copying charges, not from stamp duty. Costs payable on copies of judgements are of three kinds:-</span></span><section class=\"akn-paragraph\" id=\"section_551.a\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/98111920/\">(a)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">Court-fees payable on the application for copies,</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-paragraph\" id=\"section_551.b\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/82266502/\">(b)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">Court-fees payable when the copies are filed, exhibited or recorded in any Court of Justice (Section 6 of the Court-fees Act),</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-paragraph\" id=\"section_551.c\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/23867767/\">(c)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">the charges for making the copies. These charges are not Court-fees although for the sake of convenience they are levied by affixing equivalent Court-fee stamps to the copies (Part V, Chapter 26, Rule 641).</span></span></section><span class=\"akn-wrapUp\"><span class=\"akn-p\">In order to give effect to the provisions of Section 371, items (a) and (b) have been remitted [vide items 13 (c) and (d) and 17 in Rule 550] on copies of judgements delivered to an accused in cases other than summons cases, on copies of judgements delivered to an accused who is in jail in summons cases, and on copies of the heads of charge to the jury delivered to an accused, and item (c) has been remitted in similar cases [vide Part V, Chapter 26, Rule 641). It should be carefully noted that the remission of item (c) in Part V, Chapter 26, Rule 641 applies to copies of documents other than those laid down above, e.g., to final orders in cases under Sections 108 to 110 of the Code of Criminal Procedure, but no corresponding remission of items (a) and (b) has been made in connection with those documents and care should be taken that the correct fees are recovered.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_552\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/178769522/\">552.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">Under Section 424 of the Code of Criminal Procedure the provisions of Sections 368 to 373 of the Code apply to the judgements of Appellate Courts other than the High Court. The observations in Rule 551 consequently apply to judgements of Appellate Courts and an accused in a summons case who is in jail is entitled to a copy of an appellate judgement free of cost whether he has received a copy of the judgement of the Trial Court or not.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_553\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/4313453/\">553.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">Section 371 of the Code of Criminal Procedure envisages the grant of one copy to each accused and cannot be used for a demand for successive copies by the same person. In order to prevent such successive demands being met the head copyist should note on the order sheet of a case whenever a free copy is supplied under Section 371 of the Code and check whether such a note already exists when dealing with the grant of copies under that section.</span><span class=\"akn-p\">Use of Adhesive and Impressed Stamps</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_554\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/41396335/\">554.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-intro\"><span class=\"akn-p\">The following instructions on the use adhesive and impressed stamps contained in the Central Provinces Stamp Manual, Part II, page 186, are reproduced for the information and guidance of presiding officers :</span></span><section class=\"akn-subsection\" id=\"section_554.1\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/190579849/\">(1)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">A fees shall be denoted by a single stamp if a stamp of that value is printed; or if such a single stamp is not printed, by a stamp of the next lower value printed and one or more additional stamps, the selection of the latter conforming to the principle that a stamp of the next lower value printed shall be used in preference to stamps of smaller value.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-subsection\" id=\"section_554.2\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/167801411/\">(2)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">If a stamp of a particular value which should be used under sub-rule (1) is not available at the nearest treasury or sub-treasury or from the nearest stamp-vendor authorized to sell stamps of that value, the required value may be made up by the use of two or more stamps available at such treasury or sub-treasury or from such stamp vendor, a stamp of the next lower value available being used in preference to stamps of smaller value, In every such case, a certificate stating the value and number of the stamps required but not available shall be given by the treasury or sub-treasury officer or stamp-vendor, as the case may be.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-subsection\" id=\"section_554.3\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/141046741/\">(3)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">Whenever a treasury officer or sub-treasury officer finds that the stock of stamps of a particular value is surplus he may issue such stamps in preference to stamps of a higher value in order to adjust the surplus stock. Stamps issued under this rule shall be used as laid down in sub-rule (2). In every such case the treasury officer, sub-treasury officer or stamp-vendor, as the case may be, shall give a certificate stating the value and number of the stamps required but not issued in order to adjust the surplus stock.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-subsection\" id=\"section_554.4\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/87241689/\">(4)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">Any adhesive stamps used with impressed stamps shall be affixed to the impressed stamp of the highest value employed in denoting the fee.</span></span></section></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_555\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/98734976/\">555.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-intro\"><span class=\"akn-p\">The following further instructions on the use of stamps are reproduced from Part II, page 187, Central Provinces Stamp Manual, for information and guidance:-</span></span><section class=\"akn-subsection\" id=\"section_555.1\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/118101291/\">(1)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">With a view to facilitate the examination, under Section 6 of the Court-fees Act, of stamp fees paid on any document, any adhesive label or labels used in addition to an impressed stamp in order to make up the required value, should be affixed to the right hand upper corner of the first page of the document, immediately below the engraved portion of the stamp paper.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-subsection\" id=\"section_555.2\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/106970834/\">(2)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">When two or more impressed stamps are used to make up the amount of the fee chargeable under the Court-fees Act, a portion of the subject matter shall ordinarily be written on each stamped sheet. Where this is impracticable or seriously inconvenient, the document shall be written on one or more sheets bearing impressed stamps of the highest value, and the remaining stamps shall be punched and cancelled by the Court and filed with the record, a certificate being recorded by the Court on the face of the first sheet of the document to the effect that the full Court-fees has been paid in stamps. The writing on each stamped sheet shall be attested by the signature of the persons executing the document.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-subsection\" id=\"section_555.3\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/54853151/\">(3)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">Documents should be written on that side of the paper only which bears the stamp. When one or more impressed stamps used to denote a fee are found insufficient to admit of the entire document being written on the side of the paper which bears the stamp, so much plain paper may be joined thereto as may be necessary for the complete writing of the document and the writing on the impressed stamps and on the plain paper should be attested by the signature of the person or persons executing or signing the document.</span><span class=\"akn-p\">Note. - Officer should not refuse to receive documents which have not been prepared or stamped in the manner directed by the above rules. But they should impress upon parties and pleaders the necessity of observing the said rule if they wish to protect their own interests and avoid delay.</span><span class=\"akn-p\">Cancellation of Court-fee Stamps</span></span></section></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_556\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/85012861/\">556.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">The following instructions on the cancellation of court-fee stamps are adapted from the Central Provinces and Berar Stamp Manual:-</span><span class=\"akn-p\">A.-Documents furnished by a public officer</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-section\"><h3>1. Cancellation of Court-fee labels on copies, and other documents issued from public offices or Courts. - Every court-fee label attached to any copy or other document, denoting copying-fee as well as court-fees, if any, under Article 6, 7 or 9 of Schedule II to the Court-fees Act, 1870 issued from any Court or office, shall, before issue of such copies or other documents, etc., be cancelled by such officer as the Court or the head of the office may appoint for this purpose by-</h3>\n<section class=\"akn-paragraph\"><span class=\"akn-num\">(a)</span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">punching out a \"C\" hole in the centre of the left half of the label, and</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-paragraph\"><span class=\"akn-num\">(b)</span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">putting the date of issue and signature across the label, so as to extend to the paper on either side of it.</span></span></section></section><section class=\"akn-section\"><h3>2. Cancellation of Court-fee labels used for payment of stamp duty under the Indian Stamp Act, 1899. - Every court-fee label affixed under Rule 17 (e) of the Indian Stamp Rules, 1925, or Rule 18 (e) of the Berar Stamp Rules, 1922, on copies of maps or plans, printed copies and copies of, or extracts from, registers given on printed forms, certified to be true copies (e.g., true copies or extracts of baptismal, marriage and burial certificates, etc.) shall be cancelled by the officer issuing them by writing his name and date across the label.</h3>\n<span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">B.-Documents received by a public officer</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-section\"><h3>3. Cancellation of impressed court-fee-stamps. - On the presentation in any Court or office of a document written on an impressed court-fee stamps, it shall be the duty of the officer, referred to in Rule 12 below, after satisfying himself that the stamp is genuine and that the document is fully stamped, to punch out every figure head on the impressed portion. The cancellation of the stamp is then complete.</h3>\n<span class=\"akn-intro\"><span class=\"akn-p\">Note. - (1) The words \"presentation of the document\" do not include the presentation of a stamp on which refund or renewal is claimed.</span></span><section class=\"akn-subsection\"><span class=\"akn-num\">(2)</span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">It should be carefully noted that ascertainment of the sufficiency of the stamp should precede cancellation. Cancellation indicates that the cancelling officer is satisfied that the document is stamped sufficiently and is also \"properly\" stamped in other respects.</span></span></section></section><section class=\"akn-section\"><h3>4. Cancellation of Court-fee labels. - On the presentation in any court or officer of a complaint, petition, or other document bearing a Court-fee label or labels it shall be the duty of the office, referred to in Rule 12 below, after satisfying himself that the label or labels are genuine and have not been previously used, and that the document is fully stamped, to-</h3>\n<span class=\"akn-intro\"><span class=\"akn-blockList\"><span class=\"akn-item\"><span class=\"akn-num\">(a)</span><span class=\"akn-p\">punch out the figure-head of each label, leaving the amount designated untouched;</span></span><span class=\"akn-item\"><span class=\"akn-num\">(b)</span><span class=\"akn-p\">cancel each label by a rectangular metal date-stamp bearing the following inscription:-</span></span></span></span><section class=\"akn-subsection\"><span class=\"akn-num\">(1)</span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">name of the Court or office;</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-subsection\"><span class=\"akn-num\">(2)</span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">name of the place;</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-subsection\"><span class=\"akn-num\">(3)</span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">date, month and year; and</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-subsection\"><span class=\"akn-num\">(4)</span><span class=\"akn-intro\"><span class=\"akn-p\">the word \"Cancelled\";</span><span class=\"akn-p\">Violet ink shall be used with this stamp</span></span><section class=\"akn-paragraph\"><span class=\"akn-num\">(c)</span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">note on the right-hand top corner of the document, in ink, the value of the labels, which it bears, and initial such note.</span></span></section><span class=\"akn-wrapUp\"><span class=\"akn-p\">C.-Checks on the observance of the rules in regard to cancellation</span></span></section></section><section class=\"akn-section\"><h3>5. Cancellation by record-keeper. - It shall be the duty of the record-keeper of the Court or office to-</h3>\n<section class=\"akn-paragraph\"><span class=\"akn-num\">(a)</span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">examine every document which comes into his custody in order to ascertain first whether all stamps and labels have been cancelled as required by the above rules, and secondly, whether the value of the label or labels, if any, which it bears corresponds with their values as noted in the receiving Court or office, and</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-paragraph\"><span class=\"akn-num\">(b)</span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">cancel each label by a circular date-stamp bearing date, month and year and the name of the Court or office concerned.</span></span></section><span class=\"akn-wrapUp\"><span class=\"akn-p\">Black ink shall be used with this stamp</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-section\"><h3>6. It shall be the duty of the record-keeper of the Court or office to report to the officer to whom he may be immediately subordinate, every case in which he finds-</h3>\n<section class=\"akn-subsection\"><span class=\"akn-num\">(1)</span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">that the stamp has not been cancelled in the manner prescribed above, or</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-subsection\"><span class=\"akn-num\">(2)</span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">that the value of the labels on any document does not correspond with their value as noted in the receiving Court or office.</span></span></section></section><section class=\"akn-section\"><h3>7. It shall be the duty of the officer receiving a report under Rule 6 to submit the case for the orders of the District Judge or the Deputy Commissioner through the officer in charge of the record room or other head of the office.</h3></section><section class=\"akn-section\"><h3>8. In every District Court it shall be the duty of the clerk of Court once a month to satisfy himself, by inspection of the records lodged in the record room during the previous month, that the orders in Rules 1 to 5 above are being carried out.</h3></section><section class=\"akn-section\"><h3>9. In every district office it shall be the duty of the Deputy Commissioner, or an Assistant Commissioner appointed by him for the purpose, to make a general inspection of the record room, not less than once in every six months, and satisfy himself that the orders contained in the above rules are being carried out.</h3></section><section class=\"akn-section\"><h3>10. An inspection book shall be kept in the record room of every district office and in the office of the District and Sessions Judge in the prescribed form (No. XXI-13-Stamp-English) and a note shall be made therein of all inspections made under Rules 8 and 9.</h3>\n<span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">When the inspection is made by the clerk of Court or an Assistant Commissioner, the book shall be sent to the District Judge or the Deputy Commissioner, as the case may be, for information and orders.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-section\"><h3>11. The Presiding Judge of a Court, other than the District Court, where a record room is maintained, and the head of every office, other than a district office, shall arrange for a periodical inspection of the records of his Court or office as nearly as may be in the manner prescribed by Rules 8 and 9.</h3>\n<span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">D.-Miscellaneous</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-section\"><h3>12. Cancelling officer. - The duty of cancelling impressed Court-fee stamps and Court-fee labels in the manner prescribed in Rules 3 and 4 shall be entrusted to the reader of the Court or to any officer appointed thereto by the head of the office, excepting that the duty shall not be assigned to any person who is charged with the sale of court-fee stamps.</h3></section><section class=\"akn-section\"><h3>13. Destruction of punched out pieces. - The figure-heads of pieces of stamps or labels removed by punching shall be destroyed by burning or some other effective means.</h3>\n<span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">(In force with effect from the 1st April, 1941).</span><span class=\"akn-p\">General</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_557\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/141293997/\">557.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">The High Court desires to remind all presiding officers of their duty to protect the public revenue by seeing that the provisions of the Court-fees Act and the Stamp Act are properly enforced. The duty falls under two main heads, (a) of seeing that documents filed before them are properly stamped, (b) of seeing that the machinery set up to check the proper use of stamps is worked thoroughly and conscientiously by the subordinate staff. For this purpose all presiding officers must make themselves fully conversant with the law and the instructions on the point. They should see that every document presented is properly stamped and should whenever opportunity offers check the proper stamping of documents in records put up to them.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-chapter\"><h2>Chapter 23<br/>Expenses of Witnesses</h2>\n<span class=\"akn-intro\"><span class=\"akn-p\">(Rules 558 to 567 inclusive in this Chapter have been made under Section 544 of the Code of Criminal Procedure)</span></span><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_558\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/128755983/\">558.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-intro\"><span class=\"akn-p\">Subject to the instructions hereinafter contained the Criminal Courts are authorized to pay the expenses-</span></span><section class=\"akn-paragraph\" id=\"section_558.a\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/91972687/\">(a)</a></span><span class=\"akn-intro\"><span class=\"akn-p\">of complainants and witnesses, whether for the prosecution or the defence-</span></span><section class=\"akn-subparagraph\"><span class=\"akn-num\">(i)</span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">in cases prosecuted, instituted or carried on by, or under the orders of, or with the sanction of Government or any Judge, Magistrate or other public officer acting as such.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-subparagraph\"><span class=\"akn-num\">(ii)</span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">in cases in which the presiding officer considers such payments to be directly in furtherance of the public interest, and</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-subparagraph\"><span class=\"akn-num\">(iii)</span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">in all non-bailable cases;</span></span></section></section><section class=\"akn-paragraph\" id=\"section_558.b\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/10039445/\">(b)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">of witness summoned or recalled by the presiding officer of his own motion under Section 540 of the Code of Criminal Procedure (hereinafter called \"the Code\") :</span></span></section><span class=\"akn-wrapUp\"><span class=\"akn-p\">Provided that no payment shall be made to any witness on the part of Government where the expenses for the attendance of such witness have been deposited in Court under Section 216,244 or 257 of the Code.</span><span class=\"akn-p\">Explanation. - Cases instituted by police officers or other persons authorized by a municipal committee under the Central Provinces and Berar Municipalities Act, 1922 (II of 1922), or rules or bylaws made thereunder are not cases falling under clause (a) (i) of this rule.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_559\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/89333969/\">559.</a> </h3>\n<section class=\"akn-subsection\" id=\"section_559.1\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/140923183/\">(1)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">No payment shall be made by a Criminal Court on the part of Government to any servant of the Government of the Central Provinces and Berar, or to any official of Hyderabad State, or of the Governments of Madras, Bengal, the Punjab, the United Provinces, and Orissa, who is summoned to give evidence, in cases referred to in Rule 558, of facts which have come to his knowledge in his official capacity:</span><span class=\"akn-p\">Provided that the Court may pay such a witness his actual travelling expenses if the Court is situate within five miles of his headquarters and he is not in receipt of permanent travelling allowance.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-subsection\" id=\"section_559.2\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/60624038/\">(2)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">The Court shall grant a certificate of attendance in Form No. 17 on Schedule No. 1-Accounts to such witness specifying the dates on which he attended and the amount, if any, paid to him by the Court.</span></span></section></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_560\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/186520844/\">560.</a> </h3>\n<section class=\"akn-subsection\" id=\"section_560.1\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/117144277/\">(1)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">Expenses paid under Rule 558 may include (a) a subsistence allowance and (b) a travelling allowance.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-subsection\" id=\"section_560.2\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/102801450/\">(2)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">The subsistence allowance will vary according to the status of the witness and for this purpose witnesses are divided into three classes as follows:-</span><span class=\"akn-p\">Class A. - Persons of the labouring, Class.</span><span class=\"akn-p\">Class B. - Artisans, cultivators, shopkeepers and others of similar status.</span><span class=\"akn-p\">Class C. - Persons of superior rank.</span><span class=\"akn-p\">The District Magistrate of each district shall fix for his district maximum rates of subsistence allowance payable for each class which rates shall not exceed the following:-</span><span class=\"akn-p\">Class A- In Nagpur, Wardha, Amraoti, Akola, Buldana, Yeotmal and Khamgaon towns-Twelve annas a day;</span><span class=\"akn-p\">Class B- Re. 1 and annas eight a day;</span><span class=\"akn-p\">Class C- Rs. 5 a day;</span><span class=\"akn-p\">and the Courts may allow subsistence allowance at such rate not exceeding the district maximum as is appropriate to the circumstances of each witness.</span><span class=\"akn-p\">Note. - A servant of the Government of the Central Provinces and states summoned to give evidence, in cases referred to in Rule 558, of facts other than facts which have come to his knowledge in his official capacity shall not receive any allowance under this rule but is entitled to be paid travelling allowance as provided in the next succeeding sub-rule.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-subsection\" id=\"section_560.3\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/49432306/\">(3)</a></span><span class=\"akn-intro\"><span class=\"akn-p\">Travelling allowance may be granted, having regard to the distances to be traversed and the position and circumstances of the witness, at the rates specified below:-</span></span><section class=\"akn-paragraph\" id=\"section_560.3.a\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/195290254/\">(a)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">For journeys by road, the actual expenses incurred up to a maximum of four annas a mile provided that travelling allowance shall not be paid to A class witnesses unless through age or physical infirmity they are unable to reach the Court on foot or unless they perform the journey by public motor vehicles.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-paragraph\" id=\"section_560.3.b\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/195672057/\">(b)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">For journeys by rail to A class witness 3rd class railway fare, to B class witness 2nd or intermediate class railway fare in the discretion of the Court, to C class witnesses 1st or 2nd class fare, or, where there are no 1st and 2nd classes, upper class fare, plus 3rd class fare for one servant in the discretion of the Court.</span></span></section></section></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_561\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/152418911/\">561.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-intro\"><span class=\"akn-p\">Patwaris in the Central Provinces summoned to give evidence of facts which have come to their knowledge in their official capacity in cases referred to in Rule 558 in Courts situate outside their circles shall, if not on duty, be paid expenses in accordance with Rule 560, and if on duty shall be entitled only to travelling allowance at the rates following, notwithstanding the operation of Rule 560 and shall not be entitled to any subsistence allowance:-</span></span><section class=\"akn-paragraph\" id=\"section_561.a\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/65532448/\">(a)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">For journey by rail-single fare of the lowest class.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-paragraph\" id=\"section_561.b\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/190498165/\">(b)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">For Journey by road of not less than 10 miles-Two annas per mile from the headquarters of their circle to the destination, provided that, when they travel by motor vehicle plying for hire and the fare is less than the mileage admissible, they shall be paid an amount equal to the fare actually paid.</span></span></section></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_562\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/24152646/\">562.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">Patwaris in Berar summoned to attend as witnesses in cases referred to in Rule 558 in Courts situate outside their circles shall, whether on duty or not, be paid expenses in accordance with Rule 560.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_563\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/101920327/\">563.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">A special allowance may in the discretion of the Court be given to witnesses other than Government servants following a profession.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_564\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/62165173/\">564.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-intro\"><span class=\"akn-p\">When the Examiner of Questioned Documents or his Assistant appointed by the Central Government is summoned in criminal cases mentioned in Rule 558 no subsistence or travelling allowance shall be paid to him but a sum of Rs. 185 shall be deposited in the treasury under the head \"XLVI-Miscellaneous-Central-Other fees, fines and forfeitures-Fees for the services of the Government Examiner of Questioned Documents\" and in addition the following shall be paid by book adjustment and credited to the head \"XLVI- Miscellaneous- Central- Other fees, fines and forfeitures-Recoveries on account of travelling allowance of the Government Examiner of Questioned Documents and his establishment\":-</span></span><section class=\"akn-paragraph\" id=\"section_564.a\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/40311865/\">(a)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">Rs. 5 for the officer and 3 annas for his peon for each day of the period the officer is likely to be away from his headquarters.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-paragraph\" id=\"section_564.b\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/198880230/\">(b)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">1 \u2157 highest class railway fare for the officer and one lowest class railway fare for his peon for so much of the journey as is by railway, and eight annas a mile and one anna a mile respectively, for so much as is by road.</span></span></section><span class=\"akn-wrapUp\"><span class=\"akn-p\">The above charges shall be debited to the head \"27-D-General Establishment-Countersigned Contingencies-Diet-money and travelling allowance of witnesses\".</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_565\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/37005571/\">565.</a> </h3>\n<section class=\"akn-subsection\" id=\"section_565.1\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/93265998/\">(1)</a></span><span class=\"akn-intro\"><span class=\"akn-p\">When the Government Examiner of Questioned Documents appointed by the Provincial Government is summoned in a criminal case referred to in Rule 558, he should be paid fees as follows:-</span></span><section class=\"akn-paragraph\" id=\"section_565.1.i\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/72744309/\">(i)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">Rs. 15 for the first group of five specimens of hand-writing examined in respect of each person.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-paragraph\" id=\"section_565.1.ii\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/31350367/\">(ii)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">Rs. 2 for every specimen of handwriting of the same person examined in excess of the first group of five.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-paragraph\" id=\"section_565.1.iii\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/84913683/\">(iii)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">Rs. 8 for a photograph.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-paragraph\" id=\"section_565.1.iv\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/6898752/\">(iv)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">Rs. 16 for the first day of giving evidence and Rs. 10 for each subsequent day.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-paragraph\" id=\"section_565.1.v\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/152996105/\">(v)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">Rs. 10 for appearance on a day fixed for his evidence where his evidence is not taken.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-paragraph\" id=\"section_565.1.vi\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/54608491/\">(vi)</a></span><span id=\"section_565.1.vii\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/108930872/\">(vii)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">Rs. 16 for appearance in an appeal.</span></span></section></section><section class=\"akn-subsection\" id=\"section_565.2\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/65829912/\">(2)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">The fees specified in sub-rule (1) are exclusive of travelling allowance. When the Examiner is required to leave his headquarters in order to give evidence or for any other purpose, he shall be entitled to travelling allowance as for a Government servant drawing pay of Rs. 350 per mensem and above but less than Rs. 500.00 per mensem for journeys on tour and to daily allowance at Rs. 3 per day.</span></span></section></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_566\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/141032710/\">566.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-intro\"><span class=\"akn-p\">The Court ordering payment under these rules shall decide-</span></span><section class=\"akn-paragraph\" id=\"section_566.a\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/68104652/\">(a)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">the class to which the complainant or witness belongs and the rate at which he is to be paid, subject to the highest district rates referred to in sub-rule (2) of Rule 560;</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-paragraph\" id=\"section_566.b\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/171501132/\">(b)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">the number of days to be allowed for the journey to and from the Court.</span></span></section></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_567\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/14493625/\">567.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">In cases in which parties are required to deposit the reasonable expenses of Government servant before summoning them the following instruction shall be followed:-</span><span class=\"akn-p\">In cases in which the Government servant gives evidence of facts which have come to his knowledge in his official capacity the whole deposit and in cases in which the Government servant gives evidence of facts which have come to his knowledge otherwise than in his official capacity, the balance after paying to the Government servant travelling allowance at the rates specified in rule 560 shall be credited to Government under the head \"XXI-Administration of Justice-Miscellaneous Fees and Fines.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_568\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/135108028/\">568.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">When a private person desires to summon an officer of the Security Printing Press, Nasik Road, the Court concerned should ascertain from the officer or from the Security Printing Press Officer his pay and travelling allowance and should direct the person to deposit the fees necessary to cover the pay and allowance.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_569\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/99390657/\">569.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">The following reciprocal arrangement has been concluded between the Government of the Central Provinces and Berar and the Governments of Madras, Bengal, the Punjab, the United Provinces and Orissa in regard to the payment of amount on account of pay and travelling allowances of an officer of commercial department whose services have been requisitioned as a witness or of any other officer whose services are requisitioned as a technical or expert witness, before criminal courts, namely:-</span><span class=\"akn-p\">The pay of the officer concerned for the period of his absence from headquarters and the travelling allowance and other expenses due to him will be borne by the Government which requisitions his services, the travelling allowance being regulated by the travelling allowance rules of the Government to which he belongs. The charge in the first instance will be borne by the Government to which he belongs and then passed on after audit to the requisitioning Government.</span></span></section></section></section><section class=\"akn-part\"><h2>Part IV \u2013 Chapter 24</h2>\n<span class=\"akn-intro\"><span class=\"akn-p\">Court Registers</span><span class=\"akn-p\">(The rules in this Chapter have been made under Section 224 of the Government of India Act)</span></span><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_570\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/151488900/\">570.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">The following registers shall be maintained in the form and by the Courts shown against each in columns (3) and (4) of the subjoined table.</span><span class=\"akn-p\">The registers should be kept from year to year until and unless required by any rule or standing order to be closed at the end of each calender year:-</span><span class=\"akn-p\">Table</span><div class=\"akn--table-container\"><table class=\"akn-table\" data-eid=\"att_1__part_IV__sec_570__table_1\" id=\"att_1__part_IV__sec_570__table_1\">\n<tbody><tr class=\"akn-tr\">\n<td class=\"akn-td\"><span class=\"akn-p\">S. the Court of Session of the sessions division. Consequently Additional Sessions Judges need not maintain separate sets of registers, one set only being maintained for all the Judges of the Court.</span><span class=\"akn-p\">Note 2. - Additional District Magistrates shall maintain separate sets of registers.</span><span class=\"akn-p\">Note 3. - Courts of Session and Courts of appeal or revision should open registers as occasions arise. It is not necessary to maintain blank registers.</span><span class=\"akn-p\">Note 4. - Judges of Courts of Session should use the Book of Receipts for Money, Cause List and Inspection Book maintained by them in their capacity as Civil Judges and need not maintain such registers separately on the criminal side.</span><span class=\"akn-p\">Note 5. - Each register should bear a label showing (a) the name of the Court to which it belongs, (b) the name of the register, (c) the dates of the first and last entries, as for instance \"From 3rd November, 1940 to 17th August, 1941.\"</span><span class=\"akn-p\">I.-Register of Original Cases</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_571\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/49509400/\">571.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">In this register shall be entered all cases of prosecution for offences instituted against accused persons which are not hereinafter specified as coming under the head \"Miscellaneous\". Cases shall be numbered and entered in this register as soon as instituted. In State cases the entry in column 3 will be \"State\". In order to facilitate the preparation of the annual returns a note in red ink shall be made in the column of remarks against all offences relating to coin.</span><span class=\"akn-p\">If separate proceedings under Section 512 of the Criminal Procedure Code, hereinafter called \"the Code\", are taken against a sole accused or against one or more of several accused, a note of the fact and of the number of the case in the Register of Miscellaneous Proceedings shall be made in the column of remarks.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_572\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/38373897/\">572.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-intro\"><span class=\"akn-p\">The following instructions indicate what is meant by the term \"instituted\":-</span></span><section class=\"akn-paragraph\" id=\"section_572.a\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/58530655/\">(a)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">Cognizable cases investigated by the police of their own motion will not be regarded as \"instituted\" until the accused person is produced in custody or surrenders to his bail on the day fixed for his attendance and for the attendance of the witnesses in the case (Sections 170 and 173 of the Code.)</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-paragraph\" id=\"section_572.b\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/150847610/\">(b)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">Similarly the case of a person forwarded to a Magistrate for enquiry or trail in respect of offences committed before other Courts (Sections 476 and 482 of the Code) and the case of a person arrested and sent before a Magistrate by an authorized Revenue Officer will not be regarded as \"instituted\" until the accused is produced before the Magistrate or until the Magistrate issues process to compel his appearance, whichever may be the earlier.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-paragraph\" id=\"section_572.c\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/109402747/\">(c)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">Cases of which a Magistrate takes cognizance upon a complaint under Section 190(1) (a) or without a complaint under Section 190(1) (c) of the Code will not be regarded as \"instituted\" until the Magistrate orders the issue of a process against the accused person.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-paragraph\" id=\"section_572.d\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/90165438/\">(d)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">When a case is received from another Court, e.g., under Section 192, 346, 347, 348, 349, 526, 528 or 562 of the Code, or under Section 9 or 31 of the Reformatory Schools Act, 1897 or under Section 5(2) of the Central Provinces Borstal Act, 1928 or under Section 5 of the Central Provinces Probation of Offenders Act, 1936, the original date of institution shall be entered in column 2 of the register and a note shall be made in the column of remarks showing the date of receipt and the Court from which it is received.</span></span></section></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_573\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/148531167/\">573.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">When after a case has been decided an order is passed in appeal or revision directing further enquiry or retrial or commitment to sessions, such further enquiry, trial or commitment shall, for all purposes, including duration, be regarded as a separate case, whether it takes place in the Court which originally tried the case or in some other Court. A note shall, however, be made in the remarks column against the new entries giving the number under which the case was originally registered and the number and date of the order of the Appellate or Revisional Court.</span><span class=\"akn-p\">II.-Register of Cases tried by the Court of Session</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_574\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/105866134/\">574.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">Cases shall be considered as instituted in the Court of session on the date on which they are committed for trial. The register shall be preserved for three years from the date of the last entry therein.</span><span class=\"akn-p\">III.-Register of Miscellaneous Proceedings</span></span></section><section 1898.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-subsection\" id=\"section_575.24\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/164713398/\">(24)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">Proceedings under sub-section (1) of Section 6 and sub-sections (1) and (2) of Section 7 of the Central Provinces Borstal Act, 1928.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-subsection\" id=\"section_575.25\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/78470542/\">(25)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">Proceedings under Sections 6, 7,19 and 20 of the Central Provinces Children Act, 1928.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-subsection\" id=\"section_575.26\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/81259454/\">(26)</a></span><span class=\"akn-intro\"><span class=\"akn-p\">Proceedings under Section 12 of the Child Marriage Restraints Act, 1929.</span><span class=\"akn-p\">A miscellaneous proceeding under Section 512 of the Criminal Procedure Code, shall be registered when-</span></span><section class=\"akn-paragraph\" id=\"section_575.26.a\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/7949836/\">(a)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">no accused has been brought to trail, or</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-paragraph\" id=\"section_575.26.b\"><span class=\"akn-num\"><a href=\"/doc/138623570/\">(b)</a></span><span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">one or more of several accused have absconded and the evidence that there is no prospect of immediately arresting the absconders cannot be obtained without inconveniently delaying the trial of the accused present in Court.</span></span></section><span class=\"akn-wrapUp\"><span class=\"akn-p\">In other cases the proceedings under Section 512 of the Criminal Procedure Code shall form part of the original case.</span></span></section></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_576\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/127078584/\">576.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">The date of institution in miscellaneous proceedings is the date on which any proclamation is published, process issued or order made, or the non-applicant appears in Court or is called upon to show cause why an order should not be made against him.</span><span class=\"akn-p\">The instructions in Rule 573 shall be applied as far as possible to the registers of miscellaneous proceedings.</span><span class=\"akn-p\">IV (I).-Fine Register A</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_577\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/196930700/\">577.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">Every fine and sum of money recoverable as a fine, e.g., fees ordered to be repaid under Section 546-A, compensation awarded under Section 250 of the Code, sums recoverable under sub-section (4) of Section 113 the Railways Act, 1890, shall be entered in this register under a separate serial number of each person from whom, it is recoverable. If it is not paid into Court at once, sufficient space shall be left after each entry to allow further entries to be made in columns 11 to 14 as successive attempts are made to realize it. All fines imposed by Courts of appeal as such shall be entered in red ink. If a fine imposed by a Court of appeal is paid immediately, an intimation of payment should be sent by that Court to the Court of first instance to enable the latter Court to make the necessary entries in its registers.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_578\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/6622809/\">578.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">A new Fine Register-A shall be opened at the beginning of each year. The first entries in each new register shall reproduce the entries of the old register in respect of sums which still remain to be realized or disbursed.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_579\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/192979988/\">579.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">Items of undisbursed compensation shall be kept on the register so long as they remain in deposit. When they lapse to Government under the rules contained in the Financial Rules, Volume I, they shall be removed from the register, a note to that effect being made in the column of remarks.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_580\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/99895001/\">580.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">It should be noted that in columns 3, 12, 20 and 23 of the register, compensation means compensation payable otherwise than out of fines. Rewards are made payable out of fines by (i) Section 16 of the Public Gambling Act, 1867 (III of 1867), and (ii) Section 13 (b) of the Opium Act, 1878 (I of 1878). In (i) the full amount of the fine when realized shall be shown in column 11, the amount of reward ordered to be paid out of it being shown in column 16. In (ii) the fine shall be credited in full on realization as the reward is charged against the Excise Department, as directed in Rule 223 of the Financial Rules, Volume I.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_581\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/174890187/\">581.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">The particulars of recovery and credit shall be posted up daily from Fine Register B. Before signing any voucher for the refund of a fine or forfeited security or for payment of compensation the Magistrate shall verify from Pine Register-A that the amount is due to the person named in the voucher and that his acknowledgment has been taken in column 24 of the register, and initial it in token of his verification.</span><span class=\"akn-p\">IV (2).-Fine Register B</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_582\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/77333802/\">582.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">All items received and credited into the treasury or paid to a railway administration are to be entered in this register each day. If a fine imposed by one Court is tendered to another Court, and accepted, it shall not be shown in the registers of the latter Court but the recovery of it shall be certified by treasury receipt or otherwise to the Court which imposed the fine.</span><span class=\"akn-p\">\"Cash securities deposited under Section 513 of the Code should also be entered in this Register and credited into treasury under the head \"Revenue Deposits\".</span><span class=\"akn-p\">[High Court Notification No. 4152, dated the 8th June, 1955].</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_583\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/39489154/\">583.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">The fine register shall be scrutinized daily by the Presiding Officer who shall initial the entries of the day.</span><span class=\"akn-p\">V.-Register of Released Lunatics</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_584\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/18582590/\">584.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">All persons released on security under sub-section (1) of Section 466 of the Code shall be entered in this register.</span><span class=\"akn-p\">VI.-Register of Appeals</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_585\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/194568454/\">585.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">A separate serial number shall be given to each petition of appeal whether such appeal be made by one of several appellants or by all of them collectively.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_586\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/140371095/\">586.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">The date on which a petition of appeal accompanied by a copy of the judgement or order appealed against is first received in any Appellate Court having jurisdiction shall be entered in column 2 of the register as the date of institution, and shall be entered unchanged as the date of institution in any Court to which the appeal may be transferred under Section 407 or Section 526 of the Code.</span><span class=\"akn-p\">VII.-Register of Revisions</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_587\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/153343148/\">587.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">All cases called for under Section 435 of the Code by a Sessions Judge, District Magistrate, or Sub-Divisional Magistrate for the purpose of satisfying himself as to the correctness, legality or propriety of any finding, sentence or order, or as to the regularity of the proceedings so far as they affect the correctness, legality or propriety of such finding, sentence or order, shall be entered in this register, whether or not any action in the way of revision is taken.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_588\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/37812556/\">588.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">No case which is examined merely in order to see how a subordinate magistrate is progressing in knowledge, or with a view to ascertaining the facts, or because the duration has been long, or for any purpose other than that of considering the correctness, legality or propriety of a finding, sentence or order, or of the procedure as affecting such correctness, legality or propriety, shall be entered in this register. If any record is deemed necessary the cases so examined may be entered in a separate note book.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_589\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/142597189/\">589.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">When an application is made on behalf of the complainant, or a revision is undertaken in the interests of the complainant or of the prosecution, the name of the complainant or the words \"State\" (as in the case may be) shall be entered in column 3 and no entry shall be made in column 4. When an application is made or the revision is undertaken in the interest of the accused, column 3 will be blank, and in column 4 shall be entered the name of each accused person in whose interest the action is taken, a separate line being given to each person. In column 6 shall be entered, each in a separate line, the names of only so many of the accused in the original case as are liable to be affected by the order passed in revision. When, therefore, the revision is undertaken in the interests of the accused the entries in columns 4 and 6 will correspond.</span><span class=\"akn-p\">VIII.-Book of Receipts for Money</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_590\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/66644222/\">590.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">A receipt shall be given for all sums of money received by the reader. The receipts are printed in duplicate and the office copy shall be made out simultaneously with the original by a carbon sheet. The original which shall bear the same serial number as the carbon copy shall be torn off at the perforated line and given to the payer as his receipt.</span><span class=\"akn-p\">IX.-Inspection Book</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_591\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/98667564/\">591.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">The entries in the inspection book shall be made in accordance with the rules in Chapter 21, Part II. When complete the inspection book shall be deposited in the record room and preserved for a period of three years from the last entry.</span><span class=\"akn-p\">X.-Register of Process Fee and Diet-Money</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_592\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/41507951/\">592.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">The reader shall enter in this register the amount of diet-money deposited on behalf of each witness to who process is to issue. The total amount shall be sent daily to the nazir along with the register, and the nazir shall sign the register in token of having received the money.</span></span></section><section class=\"akn-chapter\"><h2>Chapter 25<br/>Returns and Statements</h2>\n<span class=\"akn-intro\"><span class=\"akn-p\">(The rules in this Chapter have been made under Section 224 of the Government of India Act).</span><span class=\"akn-p\">A.-Magisterial Returns</span></span><section class=\"akn-section\" id=\"section_593\"><h3><a href=\"/doc/177172263/\">593.</a> </h3>\n<span class=\"akn-content\"><span class=\"akn-p\">The following returns and statements shall be prepared by the reader of a Magistrate's court in the form shown against them:-</span><div class=\"akn--table-container\"><table class=\"akn-table\" data-eid=\"att_1__part_IV__chp_25__sec_593__table_1\" id=\"att_1__part_IV__chp_25__sec_593__table_1\">\n<tbody><tr class=\"akn-tr\">\n<td class=\"akn-td\"><span class=\"akn-p\">S. class=\"akn-p\">V-21</span></td>\n</tr>\n<tr class=\"akn-tr\">\n<td class=\"akn-td\"><span class=\"akn-p\">6.</span></td>\n<td class=\"akn-td\"><span class=\"akn-p\">Memorandum of pending
